text:
I made a test run on this recipe before company came for Christmas. It was good, but I wasn't as big a fan of that much Swiss cheese. So for Christmas I used 3/4 cup Swiss and 2 1/2 cups cheddar cheese and added green pepper for extra flavor. Everyone raved about it! It was sooo good. One thing I also did differently the second time is fry the bacon in strips and then crumble. The first time the pieces wouldn't fry completely and were stacked on top of each other, so they turned out half crisp, half soggy. It worked much better to cook them in strips and then fry the onion in a little bit of the grease afterwords.

text:
This recipe was fabulous.  I made 2 casseroles for 6 people.  I made one of the casseroles bacon & the other sausage.  The bacon one was gone first.  Though the sausage one was delicious, the bacon one was clearly the hit.  Everyone enjoyed a second helping.  I believe it is the cottage cheese & swiss cheese that make this recipe.  I followed the recipe perfectly.  I made no changes to the ingredients, however, I did broil the casseroles for 5 minutes at the end of the baking cycle to brown the top.  The next morning when my guests awoke, I said lets go to breakfast...but they requested we have leftover breakfast casserole instead!  There was plenty leftover to feed everyone again & it reheated beautifully.

text:
This is the first time I have ever rated a recipe and it is only because this recipe was so good.  This has been the breakfast cassorole that I have been looking for over the years.  I do not know if it is the swiss cheese and the cottage cheese combo or what but it is wonderful.  I did vary it a little just because of my own taste.  I used southern style potatoes and seasoned them not only with salt and pepper but also with a little cayenne pepper and garlic salt.  I also added one more egg just to extended the recipe a little further and the last item I changed is instead of bacon, I used sausage.  The changes I made really reflect my own taste.  Again this was the best breakfast recipe I have ever found!

text:
This is a wonderful recipe! I love how easy it is! I made it for guests and it got a lot of great comments. The swiss cheese really adds a nice taste to the dish. My son doesn't really care for straight egg frittatas but really enjoyed this one with the added potatoes and asks for it a lot now. I wanted to make it more often yet didn't really want to keep frozen hash browns as a staple in my house. I found out that using a couple cold baked potatoes from a previous meal and grating them (this is very easy when they are cold - I even leave the skins on them!), works even better than the frozen ones! I just plan to make a couple extra baked potatoes the day before I make this for breakfast. We also use pre-cooked turkey bacon in place of the regular bacon and it turns out great. Thanks for the wonderful recipe!

text:
I must have read all 227 reviews over and over the past couple of weeks before deciding on this dish for Easter Brunch.  Well, the company is gone and as most reviewers agreed, this dish was a hit. I wanted to post my review while my impressions were still fresh.  I had made up my mind to go with additional eggs right from the beginning based on other reviewers comments and started with 10. But once I began to mix everything together I decided to throw in a couple more eggs bringing the total to 12 and cannot see how you can possibly use less eggs. Less eggs and it would be a potato casserole. I also used only 3 cups of hash browns using the Simply Potatoes Southwest Style refrigerated hash browns and elimated the medium onion the recipe called for.  I only added a little pepper because cheese and bacon are pretty salty on their own. I prepared it the night before and let it come to room temp in the morning which was perfect. What a time saver.  I think next time I would like to try spreading the potatoes on the bottom of the pan as one reviewer suggested and pouring the egg mixture on top. This is really a great dish.... very delicious and truly a 5 star brunch casserole.

text:
I made two of these for my annual Christmas brunch this year.  For both, I first sauteed  a chopped green and a chopped red pepper with the onion for color and flavor.  For one casserole I used 1/2 pound each bacon (which I fried by itself and then cooled and crumbled) and breakfast sausage which I browned first.  For the other casserole I did a veggie version using a ton of sliced mushrooms sauteed in butter and a large shredded zucchini.  Other than that I followed the recipe exactly, using a really fantastic Jarlsberg swiss since my husband and I love swiss cheese so much (oh and since I made two I cooked for them at the same time for one hour).  Both versions were excellent and made a fantastic offering to veggie and meat eaters alike.  I served along side brie en croute, fresh cut fruit, bacon, orange juice, coffee, an assortment of Christmas cookies and my handmade truffles. Every year I try something different but I think I'll include one version of this casserole from now on.  I think they'd be great baked up in well-greased muffin tins for individual servings as well!

My family loves this.   It is so much easier to cook the bacon if you cut it into little pieces first -- I use kitchen shears to cut across the short end of the bacon.  It cooks faster & then you don't have to deal with crumbling it while it is hot.

text:
Ahhh, thank you Beth!   Finally a breakfast casserole without bread (this is also a gluten free casserole!).  Some observations.   First, the serving size of this recipe (AS WRITTEN) is off... it's not 12, it's 6 servings.  Even though it's in a big pan, it's thin.   Also, some reviewers say the hash browns don't get done, which is true if you are using the packaged FRESH hash browns in the dairy section.  The recipe calls for FROZEN hash browns which are not as thick as the fresh.  Also, don't forget to increase your bake time if you add 6 more eggs (which it really does need, or the name of this recipe would need to be changed to potato casserole).  Mine needed a total of 50 mins on 350, and it was not dry at all.  One last tip -- if you like more bland type food this is for you.  However, I needed more flavor, so I used spanish instead of sweet onion, added shallots, diced fire roasted tomatoes, dry mustard, and used 2 pounds of bacon.   All of this while still using the original 4 cups of potatoes.   Freezes very well, and I take a square to work for breakfast every day... soooo good.  Thanks for the great recipe  :-)

text:
The whole family LOVES this breakfast casserole. We did as many other reviews suggested and used 12 eggs.   We love the versatility of the recipe - it'll work with any meat or cheese you have around. We've made this several times with either ham, bacon, or breakfast sausage. Also, we've used mozzarella instead of swiss at times.   Can be made and refrigerated the night before, but it will take longer to bake if you put it in the oven right from the fridge, so allow some extra time.

text:
This was truly fantastic! I made it for my in-laws' visit at Christmas, so I needed something quick, tasty and presentable. I used leftover bacon that I just chopped up and then sauteed with the onion (and added garlic). I was really afraid of the cottage cheese because we aren't big fans of it plain but decided to go for it. You can't tell it is there but the flavor is amazing, so don't leave it out! I also added chili powder and really liked the "pop" it gave. My cheese preference was half Cheddar and half Colby Jack, with some Parmesan just for fun. Also, for lack of time, I used pre-shredded potatoes (found in the egg section).  I made this the night before and cooked it in the morning, which added about 15 minutes to the cook time.  Super versatile, easy to prep, can make ahead and tasty!

text:
This was awesome!  I stayed as close to the original recipe as I could with a few minor changes to suit personal taste.  Neither my husband or I care for onions, so I omitted them and instead used 1/2 t. onion powder to add flavor.  I also added 1/2 t. ground black pepper and 1/4 t. salt.  I added these to the egg mixture before adding the remaining ingredients.  I saw that many people were adding, sometimes DOUBLING, the amount of eggs, but I decided that with so many good reviews from people who cooked this "as is" I would give it a go without this change and stuck to 6 eggs.  It turned out lovely!  However, I do think the next time I make this (there will be a next time, it was very yummy!) I will add two more eggs.  With 6 eggs you get a faint hint of egg flavor and both my husband and I agreed this would be even better with just a bit more egg to suit our personal taste.  I recommend trying this recipe out making only minor changes for personal taste and preference, then judge for yourself if further changes are needed.  I can't imagine this being nearly as good with a full dozen eggs!  It was excellent "as is".  Definately a keeper and a nice switch from the typical strata recipe!

text:
I've made this recipe in many different versions. This is a fabulous  basic recipe to start though. That's why I gave it 5 stars.

I always use the Ore Ida O'Brien hash browns. I usually cook those in a pan with a bit of oil and onions. I like to get them crisp first. I don't like soggy potatoes in my casserole. I cut up a couple pieces of ham steak, shred some sharp cheese and a little swiss cheese. I never have used the cottage cheese. My family dislikes it. I mix all of that with 8 eggs and just dump it in the greased 9x13 pan. Sometimes I make it the night before and bake it in the morning. If I do that then I'll bake it about an hour at 350 degrees. If I bake it right away I bake it about 50 minutes. If I happend to have leftovers......not often, I'll cut it up and freeze it in thin strips to use for fast breakfast burritos on the go or a quick sandwich between toasted English Muffins. My family loves the recipe. Especially for special holidays like Christmas and Easter morning. I've also made it for dinner which they all seem to love after a long day at work and school. Thanks for the basic recipe Beth!!

Just a hint for the bacon - when I am making breakfast casseroles etc that require the bacon to be crumbled or diced up - I find it easier to slice the bacon before I cook it...then I just dump it in the frying pan and keep stirring it and use a slotted spoon to remove from the grease. I just find it alot easier than flipping strips and not being able to fit a whole pound of bacon in the pan at once. Just my two cents worth - this recipe looks awesome! I am making it this weekend!

Good but not great.  Doubling the eggs is a must or else you'll get one stiff casserole.  I made it to a T the first time - too stiff and too much hash browns.  The 2nd time, I doubled the eggs and used only 3 cups of hash browns.  This yielded a more tender casserole.  Using sausage in the casserole and sprinkling chopped cooked bacon on top makes a tasty and good looking dish.  I will make again with the revisions.

text:
I cooked the bacon and prepared/assembled everything in the greased baking dish the night before, and baked it in the morning and it turned out perfectly.  That was a great morning time-saver.  When doing it this way I took the dish out of the refridgerator about 15 minutes before putting it in the oven to take some of the chill off, and I also baked it for the full 40 minutes since it was oviously cold going into the oven.  It turned out perfectly and done throughout and everyone loved it.  I served this with hot buttered coissants, and mimosas and it served 5 people easily plus left plenty of leftovers for at least 4 more people. It's great as leftovers too.  I will try this with breakfast sausage the next time just to see which way works better.  Susage needs to be cooked and drained throughly to render the fat out of it and prevent the casserole from becoming too greasy.  This is a great recipe as is, I did not change a thing other than assembling it the night before.  Will definitely make again!

text:
I just made this recipe this morning for my Husband's birthday. I wanted something special for breakfast that I don't usually make. I've never made a breakfast casserole before and this came out AWESOME! I made some small changes, which anyone can do, it's the beauty of dishes like this... you can tweak it in many ways to your liking.   All I changed was adding a couple more eggs (8 total-I wanted leftovers), I also added a bit of chopped spinach- glad I did, it looked beautiful... and instead of onion (Hubby hates reg. onions) I used onion powder and a little chopped green onion.  I do, however, agree with other posters that say this dish does NOT feed 12. There is only 2 of us, I used this as the main dish w/english muffins, and my Hubby ate a huge piece. So, I would seriously recommend that this 12 servings only serves 5-6 adults if it's the main dish. And let's hope they aren't all men with big appetites! I'd say it would serve 8 women and maybe 5-6 men.  Now if it's just part of a big breakfast meal or you're all light eaters, then sure you can cut it into 12 decent size servings. (and remember I used 8 eggs too!)   This will be a staple for me now, I'm so happy I found this recipe... home run on the first try!

text:
Oh. My. God.  DELICIOUS!!!  I made this for dinner as a trial run for Christmas morning and it was amazing (and amazingly easy)!!!  I used 1 lb. turkey bacon instead of regular bacon; there was less bacony flavor, as expected, but it was still yummy!  I used 1 large onion; I'd halve that next time as the dish was very oniony, which might not appeal to some.  I baked it for 45 minutes as it was still "wet" at 30 and 35.  It was even better the 2nd day and made for a yummy breakfast.  I made it into 8 servings; 12 seemed too small, unless there were a few side dishes.  Best of all, LiveStrong's recipe builder puts this at 447 calories per serving (at 8 servings, with turkey bacon).  Yummy and healthy; yay!
****
12/25/10: UPDATE.  Made 2 of these for Christmas, one with bacon, one with chopped up Italian sweet sausage.  Christmas Eve local hash brown shortage forced a change to Southern style hash browns (cubed potatoes) and chopped up tater tots.  Used 2 cups tots and 2 cups hash browns in lieu of 4 cups shredded hash browns; liked the outcome better!!!  LOTS of compliments and requests for a repeat performance.  :)

I usually make this for dinner rather than breakfast, and my husband loves it.  We're vegetarian, so I replace the bacon with either Morningstar sausage crumbles or homemade seitans ground up and seasoned with herbs de Provence, depending on what I have on hand.  I omit the Swiss cheese since I'm not a fan of it and use non-fat cottage cheese.  I don't bother thawing the hash brown potatoes very well, but it's never given me a problem.  A good casserole to make if you have house guests too since you can make it the night before and serve it for breakfast, and any leftovers reheat well.

text:
We absolutely loved this recipe! After reading reviews, I kept seeing people say that it was a bit bland. Since I am from the South and I definitely need some flavor, I changed it up a bit. I wanted this casserole to be more of an omelette-type, so I used 11 eggs instead of the 6. I can't imagine using any less. I also chopped up a green pepper and put it in the food processor until it came to a very fine puree. I also added a pound of hot Italian sausage since we are meat lovers. Also, instead of the shredded house browns, I opted for 3 cups of the diced potato hashbrowns. If you like just a hint of potato, I highly recommend this. I then baked it on 350 for 40 minutes and then broiled on high for 10 minutes. It came out perfect and with all the flavor that I was looking for! I will definitely be making this again!

text:
Eating this as I type! I changed it up.  I used 8 slices extra thick bacon, 8 maple sausage links, 1/4 cup small diced ham, 2 cheeks from a green pepper, one cheek from a red pepper and  a yellow pepper, 7 eggs and 2 tbls asiago cheese. Everything else I left the same. 
Diced the peppers and onions. Cooked the bacon in strips and also cooked the sausage in separate pans. Once they were cooked I shredded the bacon and chopped up the sausage and set aside. I then drained some of the bacon fat and cooked the peppers and onions in the same pan that I cooked the bacon. After the veggies were done I added them to the already combined cheeses and potatoes. Then I added the meats and combined all of it. After scrambling the eggs in a bowl I added Paula Deen's House Seasoning to them. Then I poured them into the potatoes and mixed it all up while adding lots of black pepper and a little salt. I also added some of the soft fatty bacon to the top so it would get crispier in the oven. I baked it for 42 minutes until it was still gooey (from the cheese-not the eggs). I think many that feel the dish needs more eggs probably cooked it a little too long and the eggs and cheese got dry.  Mine still continued to cook as it sat waiting for it to settle. It was absolutely perfect by the time I cut and served. Next time I plan to use less cheddar because I am not a big cheddar lover in dishes anyway. Next time: american, mozzerella, and Tone's Cajun Seasoning! We loved this!

Sounds great as written, but I modified it based on what I had on hand.  Used defrosted hash brown cubes instead of shreds, ground breakfast sausage liberally seasoned with poultry seasoning as it was cooking, and a combination of cheddar and mexican cheese blend.  Added garlic powder, onion powder, salt, and pepper to the egg mixture.  Added a handful of cheese shreds to the top with 20 mins left to bake.  Made 1/2 recipe for my husband and I (we ate more than 1/2 of it in one breakfast!), baked in a deep round dish for about 38 mins.  Came out a little runny, so I microwaved our individual servings for about 45 seconds before serving.  Delicious - my husband really loved it - great for company - very forgiving, changeable recipe!

This casserole is great!  It's easy to make and I can't imagine it ever coming out inedible.  I used 8 eggs, (rather than the 6 called for) which I felt was perfect.  They blended in nicely with the potatoes, and there wasn't a lot of just random fluffs of egg.  The only other suggestion I would make would to add in some salt, pepper and other spices you like. Great starter recipe -- both me and hubby liked it, and we'll definitely be making it again!

This was easy and delicious.  I used mozzarella instead of cheddar because it is cheaper and monterey jack instead of swiss because my store was out. This is a wonderful brunch recipe.  I don't dice the bacon before cooking, but cook the strips and then crumble them into the mixture. Wonderful! I made several modifications out of personal taste. This is our FAVORITE egg dish! However, there is no way that it takes 15 minutes to prepare! You have to grate cheese, cook bacon, chop onions, crack eggs...I 4X the recipe and don't use the swiss cheese. When you brown the onions with the bacon the onions get very dark and small. I was concerned about the look and how they'd taste in the caserole~it gives a wonderful flavor! I added 3 more eggs for every 6 the recipe called for and cut the amount of bacon in half. It is Yummy as usual!! The recipe is so flexible~you can add, take out, change things to your taste and it turns out wonderfully!! All 6 of my kids, my hubby and my live in in-laws LOVE this!! It does reheat well~if you have any left over. I think I will try making it the night before and then just popping it in the oven because of the loooong prep time! Enjoy!!

I served this for New Year's Day break-fast and it was a hit with my family.  When I re-sized the recipe for only 6 servings, it said to use just 3 eggs.  I increased this to 5 and it worked out quite well.  I also made it the day before, refrigerated it overnight and then let it sit out as the oven was heating.  I used a smaller pan, approx 7x11x2, and the casserole was less than 1 inch thick.  I might choose a smaller pan the next time I make 6 servings so that it's a little thicker.  The best part was that this was very tasty and everyone had seconds!

Wowwwweeee - I loved this dish.  This is the first time I have made a breakfast casserole and this recipe was very good.  I served 5 people and I would say it would be good up to 8 (not 12 as the recipe states).  I made the recipe as is but for two things:  1)  I cooked the bacon first, then cut it up in small pieces as someone suggested because of soggyness and 2) Baked in the oven for 55 minutes instead of 40 min.  My guests loved this dish and I will make it again - and by the way it is not greasy and the cheeses were a great combination even if it sounds weird -- cottage cheese??? Who would have thought?  :)

text:
A very hearty and satisfying dish. I tweeked it a little by sub bacon for cooked bkft sausage w/onions. I also took prev sugg to add salt + black pepper (1/2 tsp each), good call on adding the seasonings as I think it helped bring the flavors together. I also added 1 tsp of dried dill weed, 1 TBSP fresh green onions (my personal choice), 1/2 tsp of salt + blk pepper at the end. It needed to cook for longer than what it called for, as it did not seemed cooked at 40 mins. I let it cook for 1 hr + 5 mins total time. Topped it w/some fresh green onions for that ahh freshness to blend w/the richness of the dish. End product was very satisfying and delicious. It's also economical if you make it to serve a lot of hungry folks, or your own sm family for several meals! I give it 4 stars for taste, next time I'll have to try it with bacon (:

The best breakfast casserole ever! I made this the night before and popped it in the oven the next morning at 375 degrees to speed up the cooking time. I cooked the bacon and sausage, removed it and then added diced onions, garlic, and bell pepper, seasoning it with chili powder, salt and pepper. I then mixed all the ingredients (I also added pepper jack cheese, and used 7 extra large eggs). I served this at work with honey muffins and Cholula (mexican hot sauce) and everyone at work devoured it. I will definitely be making this again for an upcoming wedding brunch. Thanks.

This is a fantastic breakfast casserole. I'm not a big fan of the bread type casseroles, and this was just the ticket. I followed the recipe exactly besides using 7 eggs and adding a tad of salt and pepper (based on other reviews). Don't be afraid of the cottage cheese, you will never know it is there. I did broil the casserole for a few minutes when it was finished baking just to melt the cheeses evenly on top (dind't want any cottage cheese showing or my husband wouldn't eat it!). I'm making this again this weekend for a baby shower as it is so easy. Will be intersting to see if a group of gals enjoy it as much as my husband and his friend.

text:
Very good! I have tried many breakfast casseroles with bread in it and have never really been impressed but this one impressed me! Was very worried that the amount of eggs did not seem near enough for the amounts of all the cheese and stuff, but not to worry--it turned out perfect! Used egg beaters cuz I had a lot that needed to be used up--went up to 7 eggs instead of 6, though. Used turkey bacon; was OK, but I think I might try Hot pork sausage or regular bacon next time. Used baked potatoes for it since that's what I had on hand. It cooked perfectly---those that think it's runny are probably seeing the melted cheeses. Just made it for the family this time but would be very proud to serve it at a potluck or to company! I took another reviewers advice and froze individual portions since school is about to start, it will make a quick easy breakfast for the kids (and me)!

We had this for Christmas breakfast and all really enjoyed it!  I used sausage instead of bacon and the whole bag of potatoes o'brian (country style hashbrowns with red/green peppers and onion) because the store was sold out of regular hashbrowns - reduced the onion by 1/2.  I also added an extra egg.  The peppers smelled and tasted wonderful and looked quite festive, too!  This is an awesome recipe to make ahead and refrigerate overnight.  Just bake a little while longer - maybe 10 - 15 minutes.  I served this with toasted cinnamon bread and fruit and it fed four hungry adults and two kids with a portion or two left over.

text:
Tastes delicious, but beware & don't put under broiler or if you do watch very closely! Don't make the same mistake I did. It was cooking beautifully but I only had 35 min. and I was bringing this dish somewhere so I listened to some other reviewers advice and put it under the broiler, I was thinking it would quick brown the top and speed along the cooking proccess.  It was under the broiler 6 minutes after baking for 30min. at 350 and it burned the top...I was so disappointed in how it looked I didn't serve it at the potluck.  I didn't want to waste it though so I picked off the really dark parts and still ate it...it still tasted delicious.  I will defenitely make it again without rushing it! also, I did do it slightly different.  I cooked the bacon first, then sauteed the onions and lightly browned the hashbrowns with them before adding all the ingredients together and I put in two extra eggs.

I made a veggie version that turned out excellent! I used a 14 oz package of bulk soy breakfast sausage and extra vegatables. text:
This was a winner for us. It passed the picky husband test with flying colors...he went back for seconds and then ate the leftovers for a snack later! I followed the recipe exactly. Only thing I did differently was add a few shakes of salt and pepper, and I added some green onion for color. I have honestly never eaten a breakfast casserole, so I didn't know what to expect or have anything to compare it to. I was afraid it was just going to be a glorified omelet. But the result was delicious and definitely its own dish. The potatoes and cottage cheese really make it special, in my opinion. I know some people are afraid of it being too Swiss cheese-y, but I used the listed amount and the Swiss cheese wasn't overpowering at all. It's also a very versatile dish. Next time (at my husband's request), I'm going to add diced mushroom, tomato, and sausage (our favorite omelet toppings). Simple, delicious, and satisfying!

text:
This was good, but I think there's a little room for improvement.  The bacon did not remain crispy once baked in the casserole, which was expected but still sort of disappointing.  I can see how this would lend itself much more to chopped ham or sausage (unfortunately we are not really fans of either).  Even after the full cooking time, my hash browns were a little crunchy, and I did defrost them as per the recipe.  I think this could be great if you found the right meat, (or no meat at all), and added some fine chopped veggies to the onion saute stage, such as mushrooms, broccoli, green pepper, etc.  I subbed onion powder for the onion (as my hubs doesn't like onion), but I think a real onion would have really added something.  I will make again, but like I said, I will add lots of other chopped veggies.  All in all, good flavor, just a couple of consistency issues.  The only addition I made was some black pepper.

I made a few changes to this recipe... I cooked the bacon and onions separately.  Cooking the bacon and onion together made a very greasy and almost burnt onion taste.  I cooked the bacon first the left is aside to cool while I cooked down the onions.  After the onions were cooked I chopped the bacon into little bits then added it to the rest of the recipe.  I also skipped the cottage cheese.  I don't really like cottage cheese and I really don't think this recipe needs cottage cheese.

text:
I make a breakfast vegetable casserole that we also like so i decided to incorporate the two into one. I add fresh broccoli and a diced roma tomato. I also use breakfast maple sausage.  I put the hasbrowns on the bottom, mix everything else together except the eggs and pour over the potatoes.  I add a little salt, pepper and garlic powder.  I beat the eggs in a bowl, and add 1 cup of milk and 1/4 cup of flour to the beaten eggs.  I then pour on top of mixture and bake 1 hour, I remove and add cheddar cheese on top and bake additional 10 mins uncovered.  We really enjoy this casserole.

text:
I made a mistake by shredding potatoes and adding them into the mix instead of the recipe's frozen hash browns. If you go this route, I suggest cooking the shredded potatoes on a large griddle with the diced onions and bacon grease. Otherwise, the potatoes don't cook evenly, and you get crunchy, undercooked potatoes.  Other than my mistake, the recipe was excellent. I prepped the casserole the night before and popped it into the oven in the morning. I took another's suggestion and broiled the casserole an additional five minutes to get a nice golden brown texture on top.

text:
I've made this several times and it's turned out great every time. I use a pound of sausage instead of bacon and I think it's great that way. I also use less Swiss and more cheddar (or Gruyere instead of Swiss--super yum) and it still comes out super tasty. I also usually use a couple more eggs than the recipe calls for, just because I like eggs, but with more eggs or the amount the recipe states, it still tastes great. I did find that I needed to leave it in the oven a while longer at higher elevations. Also I find that this doesn't quite set as well in a gas oven vs. an electric oven, even if cooked a little longer.

text:
This recipe is fabulous! I have been looking for a good breakfast casserole recipe that is gluten free and this is it. I made a mistake in the preparation that actually turned out well - I forgot to cook the onion with the bacon and just threw it in with the grated cheese before I realized what I had done. I just baked it with the raw onion and it gave it a really great flavor. I would do it that way again but would probably cut the onion amount just a bit. I made a double batch for eight people and there was only a small amount left. A single batch will definitely not serve twelve. I had to cook it about 15 mins. longer than your suggested time of 35 to 40 mins. as I had it in the oven with a ham. Also, I put it under the broiler for a minute or two before I took it out of the oven. Looked and tasted great!

This turned out really delicious. I put it all together the night before, and then baked it the next morning for an hour at 350. I used the sausage rather than the bacon, and cooked it in the onion. I got the frozen Ore Ida hashbrown potatoes, and let them thaw(for the most part) in the fridge. I used  Cheddar and Jack cheeses, no swiss. I did use the cottage cheese. Also, I used 10 eggs, instead of the 6 the recipe called for. So glad I added the extra egg-it needed it! Brought it to my grandparents house for breakfast the next morning, right from the oven! Yum!

text:
[Edit- 3/1/10-  Tried this recipe today with ham, broccoli, and green peppers- the best yet!]




I'm not much into breakfast food, but when a family friend passed away unexpectedly, I wanted to send more than just a spaghetti dish or something. I thought a nice breakfast casserole would be a nice, protein-filled morning dish for the family instead of a dinner dish or a cereal-or doughnut breakfast. The family absolutely loved it, and I've made it for my parents/family every once in a while even though I don't eat it. It's a huge hit every time and easy to make. I usually do half sausage and half bacon, and add green peppers and broccoli, and offer sour cream to top it with. Thank you so much for this recipe, and my family thanks you too!

This was WONDERFUL! I made one with sausage, one with bacon.  Both were equally popular with our company (though I preferred the sausage).  I used a bag of the Ore-Ida "Country Inn Creations Peppers & Onion" hashbrowns in place of the plain hashbrowns.  I also used an extra 1/4 cup of shredded Swiss cheese, since the package I bought was 1.5 cups and it was just easier to use it all.  I was suspicious that the recipe didn't call for any seasoning, and I thought it might at least need some pepper added at the table, but I was pleased to discover it didn't need anything! You could easily add some seasoning (or use seasoned hash browns) to change the flavor if you wanted, but it's certainly not necessary!

text:
I have been using this recipe for about 7 years now. At that time my my kids and hubby loved it! It has now become a requested dish at family gatherings. It is so versatile, you can make it with whatever you have on hand. I have made it with sausage, bacon (my fave), ham, and no meat at all for my newly vegetarian daughter. It's always delicious. At times I've substituted mashed up thawed tater tots if I didn't have hash-browns. I've also made it without the cottage cheese, which is still tasty but better with it. The recipe is pretty good as is. I just always cook my meat first and onion then add it to the rest. I've even recently started making this in muffin pans so we can pull it out during the week for a quick hearty breakfast. My teenagers love it and my mother in law asks me to make it for her church gatherings! Two picky groups of people, lol. It's super easy, cheap ingredients and delicious!

I made this into a main course by adding mushrooms and broccoli.  The mushrooms were sauteed with the bacon & onion (after the bacon was nearly done and the onion translucent) and then added some broccoli I had thawed.  Let that mixture cool a bit before adding to the egg/potato/cheddar cheese mixture then mixed it all up and spread it in a 10 x 9 baking dish, sprinkled a bit more cheddar on top and baked for 35 minutes.  My hubby loved it.  Don't think it would serve 12...but 6 for sure.  Should be good fried for breakfast.

Made this for the first time today, actually put it  together last night, refridgerated overnight and cooked this morning.  I used American cheese instead of cheddar....I prefer American cheese to cheddar any day....it's not stringy like cheddar and I prefer the taste of American cheese.  Like other suggestions, I added green onion and red bell pepper.  I used 12 eggs instead of 6, it just needed more "glue".  I also added on cup of whipping cream.  I agree that sausage is easier to prepare, but the bacon version is awesome.  I'm definately keeping this recipe on hand for future use.  Oh, and I really like the idea of using a muffin pan to make little "take along" servings.  I'm going to try that next time.

This was such a wonderful break from the usual sausage/egg casserole.  I used Monterey Jack instead of swiss and since I used a larger dish (11x15), I added about 1 cup more cheddar cheese than it calls for.  I also added 1 C. whipping cream to 7 extra large eggs, and used the entire bad of frozen (thawed) hash browns.  I diced 1 red bell pepper and 1 green bell pepper and sauteed those with the diced onion.  Will probably try adding some minced garlic to the onion/bell pepper mixture next time.  Baked for 1 hour at 350F.  Huge success!

WIN/WIN recipe for me.

Delicious recipe, super easy to make.  I made this for an Easter Brunch and my guests loved it.  I thought it was delicious though I did make some changes to it.  I used 1 pound breakfast sausage browned with 1/2 of a spanish onion.  The six eggs the recipe called for did not look like enough egg to me for an egg casserole so I used 10 eggs.  I also replaced the cottage cheese with ricotta cheese due to may own personal preference.  I baked it for 40-45 minutes and let it sit for about 5 minutes before cutting it.  This casserole was easy to make and came out perfect this way.  I will definately make this again and again.  It is likely to replace my old breakfast strata recipe that I've used for years.

Although I've been cooking for many years, I've never actually made a breakfast casserole before.  I was very excited to have this be my first.  I used turkey bacon and added dried parsley for a little color.  I prepped the casserole the day before, but kept the bacon/onion mixture separate from the potato/egg mixture until I was ready to place the dish in the oven the next morning, because I didn't want the crisp bacon to become soggy in the refrigerator overnight.  The bacon retained its crisp texture; I think this was a good idea.   I served this Christmas morning with biscuits and honey butter.  The casserole/biscuits were done to perfection just as we finished opening our gifts, which was very, very cool.  Thanks so much for the receipe :-)

text:
This was very good, but I only rated it 4 stars since it wasn't enough volume for a 9x13 pan with only 6 eggs.  I increased to 9, and still think it could have used some more.  The other quantities were exactly like the recipe, except that I added a tsp of seasoned salt since other reviewers had said it was bland. I used Simply Potatos has browns instead of frozen hash browns, and browned them and put them in the bottom of the pan so it would be more of a layered casserole.  I think the browning may have been unnecessary though.  Everything else was mixed together as a top layer.  I refrigerated and cooked it in the morning and it turned out great.  My only other comment is that 4 adults ate 2/3 of it as a main course at breakfast (and I had increased the number of eggs), so there's no way the original recipe would feed 12.

I will definitely make this again but will try increasing the eggs to 12.

text:
I made some modifications recommended by other reviewers. I skipped the Swiss cheese, but used a little extra of the cottage and cheddar cheeses and substituted sausage for bacon, for $ reasons, based on this week's grocery prices. The eggs played a minor role in this recipe. It was pretty tasty, and I would definitely make again (with bacon next time!), and keep fiddling around with the recipe. I agree that if this was the main course for people with healthy appetites, this might serve 6, and I might like a side of fresh fruit or sliced tomatoes. If served at a buffet or potluck, I'd cut it to make at least 12 servings, probably more.

text:
This is the first dish our Sunday School group devoured entirely.  Some had seconds and thirds.  Following is how I personalized this:  Use 3/4 cup Swiss and 2 1/2 cups cheddar cheese. Add red bell pepper. a small can of mushrooms (drained), 4 big dashes of Tabasco, and 1/16 tsp of Liquid Smoke for extra flavor. Fry / bake the bacon in strips and then crumble.  Saut the onion in a little bit of the grease afterword. Combine ingredients the night before and bake in the morning.  Broil the dish briefly after baking to get a nice look.  Best dish taken to SS.  No one ingredient overpowered the others, while making several distinct.

text:
I have made this twice and it is wonderful!  The only changes I made were to add salt and pepper (3/4 tsp. each) as several other readers recommended.  For those who say it needs more eggs, I don't think it is meant to be eggy; the eggs just hold it all together.

I made it this weekend for a potluck brunch and it went fast.  I got several compliments. I have not made it just for my husband and me because it is rather an indulgence for just the 2 of us, but several reviewers have said they freeze it in smaller portions and I am going to do that so we don't have to wait for a special occasion or a holiday next time.

text:
After reading all the reviews I made this casserole for the first time for my child's 4th grade end of year breakfast.  Knowing my kids don't like swiss cheese, I opted to use 1.5c shredded colby instead.  I also used 2c sharp cheddar.  Instead of bacon, I used 1 lb of Jimmy Dean original sausage with 1/4 of a large vidalia onion.  Instead of plain shredded has browns, I used 1 whole pkg (1lb 4 oz) ore ida country inn creations peppers & onions hash browns.  I added salt and pepper to my beaten eggs and then assembled the casserole using about 1.5c small curd cottage cheese.  I baked in a glass baking dish at 350 degrees for 50 minutes.  I was surprised when my daughter told me that everyone in her class ate some and loved it.  In fact she complained that I should have made one for us at home.  So I made another one for dinner, along with bacon and biscuits for sides...what can I say, we all enjoyed it greatly.  This will become a regular for us.

text:
If you're looking for a "healthy" breakfast casserole, you're out of luck.  This, however, is a really tasty breakfast casserole.  I was skeptical, at first, about the amount of Swiss cheese but the Swiss and cottage cheese are key to giving it a wonderful smooth, creamy texture.  I made this for a few friends at work and now I'm going to have to bring it in for everybody at our next potluck because it was so popular.  It's very simply but the taste and texture are just awesome.  It's also surprisingly not heavy so you won't wear down your whole day if you have it first thing in the morning.  Highly recommend it.

text:
This recipe is very customizable. I substituted sausage for the bacon and added habanero sauce and ground red pepper to spice it up. This recipe just begs for you to add whatever you love the most, because the potatoes/cheese mixture is a little bland by itself. Three of us ate, two had seconds, and I had plenty of leftovers to freeze in individual portions and pop out when I need a quick meal. Delicious!
